    "parent_id": "UgxBAmCQjCgGq8C7Bc14AaABAg",
    "username": "@SeniorKlean",
    "clean_text": "\"binning\" refers to metaphorical or maybe literal bins, as in containers, used to sort the chips by performance capability. all processor dies get tested for the top spec, those that pass go in the top bin. those that fail get tested for the next spec down, those that pass go into that bin. this may repeat several times. apple only does it twice. intel does it like 7 times. the percentage of dies that pass the top spec is referred to as \"yield\". one reason apple silicon tends to be expensive is that they use advanced manufacturing nodes much earlier in their development than competitors when they still have very low yield. the actual process involves using lasers and acid baths to disable certain parts of the processor die when it fails certain tests. then when the die gets bonded to the chip package some auxiliary components will get connected in different patterns to set it's speed and tell the rest of the system which model it is.",
